  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_300ff056-6e18-4391-9cb9-32b0efbb52d4'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer10577411353605208239">As the bloody Human-Covenant War rages on Halo, the fate of humankind may rest with one warrior, the lone SPARTAN survivor of another legendary battle... the desperate, take-no-prisoners struggle that led humanity to Halo--the fall of the planet Reach. Now, brought to life for the first time, here is the full story of that glorious, doomed conflict.<br/><br/>While the brutal Covenan</span>
  <span id="freeText10577411353605208239" style="display:none">As the bloody Human-Covenant War rages on Halo, the fate of humankind may rest with one warrior, the lone SPARTAN survivor of another legendary battle... the desperate, take-no-prisoners struggle that led humanity to Halo--the fall of the planet Reach. Now, brought to life for the first time, here is the full story of that glorious, doomed conflict.<br /><br />While the brutal Covenant juggernaut sweeps inexorably through space, intent on wiping out humankind, only one stronghold remains--the planet Reach. Practically on Earth's doorstep, it is the last military fortress to defy the onslaught. But the personnel here have another, higher priority: to prevent the Covenant from discovering the location of Earth.<br /><br />Outnumbered and outgunned, the soldiers seem to have little chance against the Covenant, but Reach holds a closely guarded secret. It is the training ground for the very first "super soldiers." Code-named SPARTANs, these highly advanced warriors, specially bioengineered and technologically augmented, are the best in the universe--quiet, professional, and deadly.<br /><br />Now, as the ferocious Covenant attack begins, a handful of SPARTANs stand ready to wage ultimate war. They will kill, they will be destroyed, but they will never surrender. And at least one of them--the SPARTAN known as Master Chief--will live to fight another day on a mysterious and ancient, artificial world called Halo...</span>
  <a data-text-id="10577411353605208239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Halo and Ender's Game fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16514762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7051215763634072238">Ha! A book about Halo?! ROFL.<br/><br/>I was wrong. <br/><br/>Expected this: "Grenade, headshot, headshot. Two grunts down. More grenades. 360 no scoped an Elite." etc. A book about mindlessly shooting things up.<br/><br/>Got this: A book that doesn't focus on wars or engagements, but the thoughts and emotions of the Spartan's (yes, they have emotions!). You place yourself in their shoes and they are no longer dudes who are just good at shooting things. You see the painful life of brainwashing and conditioning they've gone t</span>
  <span id="freeText7051215763634072238" style="display:none">Ha! A book about Halo?! ROFL.<br /><br />I was wrong. <br /><br />Expected this: "Grenade, headshot, headshot. Two grunts down. More grenades. 360 no scoped an Elite." etc. A book about mindlessly shooting things up.<br /><br />Got this: A book that doesn't focus on wars or engagements, but the thoughts and emotions of the Spartan's (yes, they have emotions!). You place yourself in their shoes and they are no longer dudes who are just good at shooting things. You see the painful life of brainwashing and conditioning they've gone through. They are not dumb, they think and feel. Most of all, you see how conflicted they are.<br /><br />The video game never showed this. You never "felt" what happens behind the mask. Eric Nylund did a great job of bringing these characters to life and making you "believe" in what the Spartan's believed. You feel their passion, you want them to win, and are pained by their loss.<br /><br />Instead, it reminded me of Orson Scott Card's "Ender's Game" and the idea of how you *create*, rather than recruit, elite soldiers. The books were way better than the game. I bought Halo 3 and barely played it because of the Halo book trilogy!<br /><br />To wrap up, the book also takes place before the events in the Halo video game and explains the origins of the character you play. The game made a lot more sense after reading this book. It used lots of Navy jargon and tried to sprinkle military tactics in to most of the battle situations. <br /><br />Verdict: I loved Ender's Game, and I'd place this right along side it. Solid read with some great character development. You will be a Spartan when this is over.<br /><br />Disclaimer: I played Halo 1 before reading this series which may have helped me develop a relationship with the general story and characters. Also, I didn't like the 2nd book as much (The Flood). It was written by a different author who seemed to be more of a scribe for a gamer just playing thru the game. Basically it sounded like he never played the games himself and just watched someone play them and wrote down what they did. I didn't feel the emotion nearly as much. I'd recommend playing the first Halo in place of reading The Flood as it is virtually the exact same story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7051215763634072238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2448202032?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10667530766214293526">Well, I’m doing it: I’m diving full on into the Halo universe. Games, novels, comics, web series, podcasts…I’m doing all of them, in the order that they were released. So, in other words, it was nice knowing ya’ll – I’ll see you in 20ish years.<br/><br/>I played the original Halo trilogy years ago, and distinctly remember reading the first three Halo novels that were published: “Halo: The Fall of Reach,” “Halo: The Flood,” and “Halo: First Strike.” Rereading “The Fall of Reach” almost 15 years later, I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText10667530766214293526" style="display:none">Well, I’m doing it: I’m diving full on into the Halo universe. Games, novels, comics, web series, podcasts…I’m doing all of them, in the order that they were released. So, in other words, it was nice knowing ya’ll – I’ll see you in 20ish years.<br /><br />I played the original Halo trilogy years ago, and distinctly remember reading the first three Halo novels that were published: “Halo: The Fall of Reach,” “Halo: The Flood,” and “Halo: First Strike.” Rereading “The Fall of Reach” almost 15 years later, I was impressed by just how well Eric Nylund sets up not only the events of the video game, but also the Halo universe at large: from the origins of the mankind’s war with the Covenant, to the creation of the Spartan program, to developing Master Chief into a real and distinct character, to laying out all of the ins and outs of Slipstream and humanity’s interstellar journeying…there’s a lot of ground that Nylund covers here, and he somehow does it all in a way that’s genuinely entertaining. Color me impressed.<br /><br />Next up: the original Halo videogame, followed by “Halo: First Strike” (the one and only piece of Halo material I’ll be skipping is “Halo: The Flood”, because a.) if I recall correctly, it’s more or less a pretty straightforward retelling of the Halo story, and b.) I don’t remember it being all that great. <br /><br />Onward! <br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer538127474055849568">I have played all of the Halo games and followed the story in the games and thoroughly enjoyed them. I was given this book several years ago and never got around to reading them, until I got my hands on the audio book version! <br/><br/>This book was incredible. It was not predictable at all. It begins when Master Chief was selected as a child for the Spartan program. Putting the setting well before the first Halo game. The author does a great job describing Master Chief and getting the readers following </span>
  <span id="freeText538127474055849568" style="display:none">I have played all of the Halo games and followed the story in the games and thoroughly enjoyed them. I was given this book several years ago and never got around to reading them, until I got my hands on the audio book version! <br /><br />This book was incredible. It was not predictable at all. It begins when Master Chief was selected as a child for the Spartan program. Putting the setting well before the first Halo game. The author does a great job describing Master Chief and getting the readers following his development as a strong, complex character.<br /><br />This book is not a fun, light hearted read either. Master Chief experiences some terrible things and in the end, all he has is his orders and missions that keep him focused and determined. <br /><br />I'm not much of a Sci-fi guy or a fantasy guy either, but I have to admit, this book was unlike any sci-fi book I have read. Simply awesome! A must read!!</span>

<div id="review_108567940" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108567940" />
    <a title="Claudiu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3907768-claudiu"><img alt="Claudiu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277277594p2/3907768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108567940?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudiu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudiu" href="/user/show/3907768-claudiu">Claudiu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108567940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer539735458038564647">Originally posted on: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.gametrailers.com/users/SlaveZero/gamepad/?action=viewblog&id=500509'>http://www.gametrailers.com/users/Sla...</a><br/><br/>First off, and foremost actually, I beg of you all to not believe the hype that this book has surrounded itself in. It is, by far, one of the worst Sci-Fi reads I've had in recent history and the few good things about it get eclipsed by the shoddy writing and the down right awfulness that are most of the characters.<br/>Right, let's get some structure in here.<br/><br/><b>The plague of tie-in books</b><br/><br/>Tie-in books have been around for a long time now. They</span>
  <span id="freeText539735458038564647" style="display:none">Originally posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.gametrailers.com/users/SlaveZero/gamepad/?action=viewblog&amp;id=500509">http://www.gametrailers.com/users/Sla...</a><br /><br />First off, and foremost actually, I beg of you all to not believe the hype that this book has surrounded itself in. It is, by far, one of the worst Sci-Fi reads I've had in recent history and the few good things about it get eclipsed by the shoddy writing and the down right awfulness that are most of the characters.<br />Right, let's get some structure in here.<br /><br /><b>The plague of tie-in books</b><br /><br />Tie-in books have been around for a long time now. They're that special kind of literature that bases itself more on the success of the media outlet, rather than the author's ability to weave something great. As such, whole libraries are full of 'Star Wars', 'Star Trek', 'The X-Files', 'Spider-Man', 'Men in black' and so on. And if original works were to get slapped any harder, these books are usually pushed up-front for their obvious hook. Fans will buy them, people that heard of the movies will buy them as well out of curiosity and here we go into that black hole of bad literature helped along by big names.<br /><br />I had initially expected 'Halo - The fall of Reach' to be THAT book that actually shows there's some point in picking up such a book for other reasons rather than the fact that you've loved the game.<br />High and unfair expectations one might say. But, taken the source material, a game that has really married consoles and shooters, would it not be fair to expect the book to really marry games and literature?<br /><br />But still, perhaps I went into this read with higher expectations than I was allowed for any other book. But, as my expectations are high for people like Frederik Pohl or Frank Herbert, Orson Scott Card and the illustrious Aldous Huxley, am I not to have the same expectations for a celebrated author like mr. Eric Nylund?<br /><br />But no, this work proved once again that there is still little hope for a proper union between mediums. For myself, personally, it only cements that view that there is little hope for tie-in literature, despite the illusion of world expanded and characters built upon...there simply is too little here for such grand things.<br /><br /><b>The itty gritty of bad craftsmanship</b><br /><br />Allow me to start off this bit of writing with the highs and lows of this book. It'll provide grounds to built upon.<br /><br />The pros:<br />- good idea;<br />- fun to read space battles;<br /><br />The cons:<br />- poor execution;<br />- bad, bi dimensional characters;<br />- forced attempt to tie into the game that it prequels;<br />- bad action scenes.<br /><br />I won't be fair about this, I know. But then again, I don't need to be.<br />This is bad Sci-Fi here. And it's bad for quite a number of reasons that need mentioning.<br /><br />First off, what you can't but notice as you read the first page, is the fact that this author can't write at a steady pace. He just can't. From the first page, to the last one, you need to put off with a constant barrage of character names being repeated every three phrases and the unequal pace of everything brought about by the choppy writing.<br />Now, what can it mean when you call writing 'choppy' for lack of a better term?<br />If a game stutters you can name the framerate 'choppy'...and that's a very good simile right there. 'The fall of Reach' is a bad framerate put into words and stretched on 340 pages. The action always moves either too fast or simply too slow and the flow of the phrases help worsen things.<br /><br /><i>Bla bla bla! he said moving his head.<br />He got out of the Warthog and walked to the barracks. The guard saluted. He returned the salute almost without thinking.</i><br /><br /><br />Yes, that's about it. You get used to it after fifty pages or so, but it still rears its ugly head each and every time you seem to get some real enjoyment out of the book.<br /><br />There are no real characters here.<br />The super-genius unique scientist?<br />The children being trained, of which only just four or five actually get a voice or name?<br />The serious and level headed captain?<br />The tomboyish yet incredibly smart AI?<br />The tough general barking orders?<br />All non-characters! Bland, unexciting, uninteresting and BORING. That's what all the characters in this book have amounted to.<br />It's seen as the story of how the Spartans came to be yet, except for Master Chief, every other Spartan is there for cannon fodder or to force upon us the fact that the main character wasn't the strongest or fastest (tie-in to the multiplayer anyone?) but merely the bravest. Their dialogue is laughably bland and full of extreme cliches. There's so much emphasis on some of them (as the main cast in the game) that it's easy to get unnerved seeing how some, much more interesting ones, are swept aside in the attempt at humanizing the Master Chief.<br />Which attempt, I'm sad to report, doesn't do anything to his persona. Still a bland wind-up toy soldier he remains, no matter the back story now...the book made sure of hammering out all that could be remotely human in him.<br /><br />Anywho, I'll stop hammering at this. This is simply an example of a rank amateur trying his hand at something well beyond him. I'm sure there are people out there that consider this as some sort of 'DUDE, BEST BOOK EVAH!' but seriously talking: this is rubbish. Unapologetic rubbish...<br /><br /><b>The George Lucas school of story-telling</b><br /><br />If some of you have seen the entire 'Star Wars' series of films then the above title will be more than revealing for you.<br />As bad as some of the parts are, there is still some good in this thing. I won't lie...it gets tedious and annoying each time the action concentrated on a character; but when it went into space, it really could become something interesting to read. There was some serious gold here to be dug out if the plot would've concerned some of the space battles...but, sadly, wasn't to be.<br /><br />The worst sin this books commits against itself is how badly it tries to fit before the first game. When the ending rolled about, it proved that most of the secondary characters were nothing more than sacrificial lambs on an altar of empowering the Master Chief even further, and the story of the sequels.<br />There is some geniality in the attempt at irony at the ending...but sadly, it's hamfisted and force fed to us. It doesn't shy away from it either, it's in our faces and the arms is driven deeply down our necks with the ham.<br /><br />George Lucas would be envious of how this ties in. Even his disaster wasn't as bad.<br /><br /><b>Ending</b><br /><br />What can I say in closing? Don't waste your time reading this, really, don't. There is far better Sci-Fi out there, far flashier, far more interesting. This is, at best, the equivalent of a pop-corn film: watchable but forgettable and, without the butter, quite bland.<br />I can't say the games deserved better than this...God knows, 'Halo' is not the most intriguing story-line out there...but fans deserved better than this attempt.<br /><br />I was curious for the game. Now I know that everything that was interesting in this book will be absent from the game.<br />Screw it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="539735458038564647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131474544?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131474544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12796587956664524023">This is essentially a military Sci-Fi book with echoes of both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17214.Starship_Troopers' title='Starship Troopers by Robert A. Heinlein' rel='nofollow noopener'>Starship Troopers</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375802.Ender_s_Game__Ender_s_Saga___1_' title='Ender's Game (Ender's Saga, #1) by Orson Scott Card' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ender's Game</a>. I haven't played the Halo games as I don't own an XBox, although I did dip into Combat Evolved at some stage (the one Halo that came out on PC). I remain intrigued by the concept of the Halo (a <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61179.Ringworld__Ringworld___1_' title='Ringworld (Ringworld, #1) by Larry Niven' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ringworld</a>-like structure - albeit <i>much</i> smaller). At this stage I would like to insert a comment on some of the negative reviews listed. This book is based on a video game franchise, yes, and is likely aimed </span>
  <span id="freeText12796587956664524023" style="display:none">This is essentially a military Sci-Fi book with echoes of both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17214.Starship_Troopers" title="Starship Troopers by Robert A. Heinlein" rel="nofollow noopener">Starship Troopers</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/375802.Ender_s_Game__Ender_s_Saga___1_" title="Ender's Game (Ender's Saga, #1) by Orson Scott Card" rel="nofollow noopener">Ender's Game</a>. I haven't played the Halo games as I don't own an XBox, although I did dip into Combat Evolved at some stage (the one Halo that came out on PC). I remain intrigued by the concept of the Halo (a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61179.Ringworld__Ringworld___1_" title="Ringworld (Ringworld, #1) by Larry Niven" rel="nofollow noopener">Ringworld</a>-like structure - albeit <i>much</i> smaller). At this stage I would like to insert a comment on some of the negative reviews listed. This book is based on a video game franchise, yes, and is likely aimed at a younger market or niche market. In all fairness, it can not be compared to, for example, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/234225.Dune__Dune_Chronicles___1_" title="Dune (Dune Chronicles, #1) by Frank Herbert" rel="nofollow noopener">Dune</a> for complexity. This is the kind of book that is likely to turn younger readers onto reading, especially if they've played the game, and how can that be a bad thing?<br /><br />The book itself is extremely readable. It is very well paced and I flew through it. So, no time wasted. It is also a lot of fun, and surprisingly well written, considering its roots. Like I said, I'm not a Halo-player and yet I really enjoyed this novel. Kudos to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33958.Eric_S__Nylund" title="Eric S. Nylund" rel="nofollow noopener">Eric S. Nylund</a> for taking the available back story info and crafting it into something rather promising. I'm continuing with the series, since it now has my attention.<br /><br />I would certainly recommend The Fall Of Reach to readers who enjoy military science fiction, but who will appreciate something just for the heck of it too. If you're a fan of the game, this is required reading. Great stuff!<br /><br />Edit: the edition I read (Del Rey) did have one or two grammatical errors / typos - let's hope the Tor edition coming out will have fixed that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12796587956664524023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1018540396240638098">This book is based on a video game...and it's pretty good. I was in the mood for a straight forward even simple story. Good guys vs bad guys, military space opera, aliens who want to conquer the universe, or burn it... <br/><br/>Cool.<br/><br/>Okay, so it's not Tolstoy or Dickens (not that Dickens is necessarily all that hot LOL).   <span id="freeText1018540396240638098" style="display:none">This book is based on a video game...and it's pretty good. I was in the mood for a straight forward even simple story. Good guys vs bad guys, military space opera, aliens who want to conquer the universe, or burn it... <br /><br />Cool.<br /><br />Okay, so it's not Tolstoy or Dickens (not that Dickens is necessarily all that hot LOL). But these books (there is a series based on the game) are fun, action packed and really pretty well written.<br /><br />We open with the "founding of" or "recruiting of" the Spartans. "Of course" our hero is "Master Chief" (anyone who's played the game would know that of course). At the beginning of the book we know little (or nothing) about "The Covenant". These are our "bad guys" and they'd rather destroy a planet than leave it in human hands!<br /><br />So, enjoy, read, soak up all the wonderful mindless violence. You can read something "worthwhile" later.</span>

<div id="review_1971586633" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1971586633" />
    <a title="Jeannette Nikolova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova"><img alt="Jeannette Nikolova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480677087p2/2574284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1971586633?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeannette Nikolova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeannette Nikolova" href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova">Jeannette Nikolova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1971586633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3352232207370464070"><a href='https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2017/04/26/halo-the-fall-of-reach-by-eric-s-nylund/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>Also available on the WondrousBooks blog.</i>
</a><br/><br/><em>*** 1.5 stars ***</em><br/><br/>Well... at least I tried.<br/><br/>I have a friend who is a big <strong>Halo: The Fall of Reach</strong> fan and in his attempt to get me interested in the story, he convinced me to give it a shot.<br/><br/>I really, really tried to like the story, the book, the writing... I couldn't.<br/><br/><strong>Halo: The Fall of Reach</strong> to me was poorly written and rather dreary, shallow and messy. Many events came to be in the book, but the story moved so little in terms of world-building. Yes, of c</span>
  <span id="freeText3352232207370464070" style="display:none"><a href="https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2017/04/26/halo-the-fall-of-reach-by-eric-s-nylund/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>Also available on the WondrousBooks blog.</i>
</a><br /><br /><em>*** 1.5 stars ***</em><br /><br />Well... at least I tried.<br /><br />I have a friend who is a big <strong>Halo: The Fall of Reach</strong> fan and in his attempt to get me interested in the story, he convinced me to give it a shot.<br /><br />I really, really tried to like the story, the book, the writing... I couldn't.<br /><br /><strong>Halo: The Fall of Reach</strong> to me was poorly written and rather dreary, shallow and messy. Many events came to be in the book, but the story moved so little in terms of world-building. Yes, of course there were big events, but most of them were battles between the Covenant vs Deus ex machina. And my curiosity about the essence of this world was hardly nourished.<br /><br />For starters, the core of the story were the war and the creation of the Spartans because of the war. But those two ideas were developed in such a strange way that I couldn't really make myself take the story seriously. The Spartans were described in very contrasting ways, which could make sense if developed properly (the people who support the idea of the Spartans' creation - the Spartans themselves - the horrors of their creation - the people who would like to see them fall), however the majority of these contrasts were written in a very off-hand manner, so it just seemed like that was "writing for the purpose of filling pages" in between epic battles.<br /><br />And don't even get me started with the battles. There was so much... I would say, "military jargon"? Just commands, terms, words that may make sense to gamers, but not to a casual reader... More so, however, the battles were lead solely relying on miracles, a.k.a deus ex machina. Half of the battles scenes between generic ships and ship crews went on like this:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>"- We have to fight!</em>
  <br />
  <em> - Sir, they are turning around!</em>
  <br />
  <em> - Oh no, we will die!</em>
  <br />
  <em> - At least we are going to die in honor!</em>
  <br />
  <em> - There's nothing more to do! We will die!</em>
  <br />
  <em> - UNLESS! Turn the ship, yeah, hit them Covenant bitches, uh uh, how do you like me now?!</em>
  <br />
  <em> - Oh sir, you saved us! How did you come up with this brilliant plan?</em>
  <br />
  <em> - Nah, it wasn't anything special."</em>
</blockquote><br /><br />In general I just couldn't get engaged in the story. Not my cup of tea at all, I admit, but I still thought it might surprise me. It didn't.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3352232207370464070" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_329630426" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/329630426" />
    <a title="Tina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3971007-tina"><img alt="Tina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461261523p2/3971007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/329630426?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tina" href="/user/show/3971007-tina">Tina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Halo fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tina by: </span>
      Matt and Hunt
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer329630426" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3695065094338909666">I wasn't expecting too much from this book, so I was more than surprised at the quality of the novel. It's wonderfully fun. The author has very fluid prose that keeps you addicted to the story but doesn't rush you through it. Also, given this is a prequel to the games, the author was kind of stuck writing within certain parameters, meaning that he had to conform to the series' history/locations, and he has to ensure his writing was accessible to everyone - that leaves little room for experimenta</span>
  <span id="freeText3695065094338909666" style="display:none">I wasn't expecting too much from this book, so I was more than surprised at the quality of the novel. It's wonderfully fun. The author has very fluid prose that keeps you addicted to the story but doesn't rush you through it. Also, given this is a prequel to the games, the author was kind of stuck writing within certain parameters, meaning that he had to conform to the series' history/locations, and he has to ensure his writing was accessible to everyone - that leaves little room for experimentation with regards to prose or ideological concerns. So, I forgive the very conventional format/style. <br /><br />On that note, the only real issue I had with the story was the character development. The characters were unique to themselves, but no one was very deep. The characters read like typical action-movie stars: they are likeable and their motives are very black and white. It wouldn't have detracted from the story to have more background on the characters.<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3695065094338909666" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2552289236" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2552289236" />
    <a title="The Grim Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25068072-the-grim-reader"><img alt="The Grim Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543631430p2/25068072.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2552289236?book_show_action=true">Oct 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Grim Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Grim Reader" href="/user/show/25068072-the-grim-reader">The Grim Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2552289236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1442706622552015412">As a MASSIVE fan of the HALO franchise, it’s perhaps surprising that it has taken me this long to get into the books. Maybe it’s because I’m not a huge sci-fi reader. Regardless, I decided to take the leap into space and join the Master Chief and his team of Spartan badasses on their mission to rid the universe of the Covenant threat.<br/>HALO: The Fall of Reach is the first book in the series and follows the path of John as he moves through the ranks eventually becoming the famed Master Chief. This </span>
  <span id="freeText1442706622552015412" style="display:none">As a MASSIVE fan of the HALO franchise, it’s perhaps surprising that it has taken me this long to get into the books. Maybe it’s because I’m not a huge sci-fi reader. Regardless, I decided to take the leap into space and join the Master Chief and his team of Spartan badasses on their mission to rid the universe of the Covenant threat.<br />HALO: The Fall of Reach is the first book in the series and follows the path of John as he moves through the ranks eventually becoming the famed Master Chief. This is definitely not hard sci-fi, this is pulpy action-packed reading that requires little knowledge of the game to be enjoyed though fans of the game will love the appearances of key figures from the HALO universe.<br />The book is well paced throughout. The space battles are exciting to read about particularly the early exchanges between the Covenant and the humans in which we fully understand what they are up against. The Covenant are brutal, efficient killing machines who only have one thing in mind…extermination! But even these don’t hold a candle to the scenes with the Spartans. I got goosebumps several times whilst reading about the Master Chief destroying all who cross him and his team. He really is the ultimate badass and Nylund does a great job of bringing him to life on the page whilst keeping his character faithful to the game. I was a little concerned that most of the book would focus on John’s training and that very little would feature the Master Chief. I’m pleased to report I was wrong and whilst there are certainly a few chapters dedicated to the training, I felt they didn’t drag.<br />HALO: The Fall of Reach feels like but a drip in the ocean and the scope is there to expand throughout this universe indefinitely. This book will easily please casual sci-fi readers with its full-throttle action scenes and engaging characters. I’ll certainly be exploring other books in the series. To infinity and beyond! (oh, wait! That’s the wrong character!).<br />4/5 plasma grenades from the Grim Reader</span>
  <a data-text-id="1442706622552015412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_162535884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162535884" />
    <a title="Jerome" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1332444-jerome"><img alt="Jerome" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245359822p2/1332444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162535884?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jerome" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jerome" href="/user/show/1332444-jerome">Jerome</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162535884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16193992439277665416">Mass market paperbacks covering someone else's IP must be a pain to write, since you're probably under a huge time constraint to come up with 250 pages worth of story constrained by existing canon. But even more constricting is the fact that your work is permitted to exist only to further sales of the primary product. In essence, your book is a commercial. <br/><br/>Given that, Nylund does a pretty decent job putting some life into a killing game. While the protagonist, John 117, hardly rises above the au</span>
  <span id="freeText16193992439277665416" style="display:none">Mass market paperbacks covering someone else's IP must be a pain to write, since you're probably under a huge time constraint to come up with 250 pages worth of story constrained by existing canon. But even more constricting is the fact that your work is permitted to exist only to further sales of the primary product. In essence, your book is a commercial. <br /><br />Given that, Nylund does a pretty decent job putting some life into a killing game. While the protagonist, John 117, hardly rises above the automaton of the game, here he at least has some back story, some sense of connection to his fellow Spartans, and a deep seeded drive to "win". This makes him only a little less despicable than, say, Robert Howard's Conan. But the reason you end up liking Conan is because he is better than the rest of the world he lives in. The same is true of Master Chief. He is essentially kidnapped and forced by a world-spanning government (the UN) to become a killing machine, one specifically aimed at human beings who are seeking their own autonomy through resisting UN's rule. While Nylund's account avoids explicit moral judgment regarding the insurrectionists, one can only imagine Master Chief as the moral equivalent of Darth Vader hunting down rebels or "the Operative" hunting down River Tam &amp; the crew of Serenity.<br /><br />Thankfully for the franchise, all this become moot when humanity is threated by the alien Covenant and the Evil Empire -- I mean, United Nations -- get's to serendipitously turn it's killing machines on the alien invaders. And for us, since we don't have to think about the moral quandaries, and can sit back and enjoy, since all of the violence and killing is morally good. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16193992439277665416" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_743964341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/743964341" />
    <a title="David Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15327799-david-martin"><img alt="David Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469370586p2/15327799.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/743964341?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Martin" href="/user/show/15327799-david-martin">David Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer743964341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2385460939128667534">Having gotten used to reading very deep, character driven series like Game of Thrones, it was an abrupt switch to read a novel in which character development and differentiation took a bit of a back seat to the action. That isn't the author's fault, per se, but I would be lying if I didn't say I wanted some depth added.<br/><br/>That said, God bless this guy, he wrote this book in under two months so that its release could roughly coincide with the original release of the first Halo videogame, and he wrot</span>
  <span id="freeText2385460939128667534" style="display:none">Having gotten used to reading very deep, character driven series like Game of Thrones, it was an abrupt switch to read a novel in which character development and differentiation took a bit of a back seat to the action. That isn't the author's fault, per se, but I would be lying if I didn't say I wanted some depth added.<br /><br />That said, God bless this guy, he wrote this book in under two months so that its release could roughly coincide with the original release of the first Halo videogame, and he wrote the book within a universe that was still being developed as he wrote it. So hats off for creating a generally compelling novel under duress.<br /><br />The battles, which drive much of the story, are predictable: set up the impossible odds of a battle, and allow a couple of clever moves overcome those odds. Like many such stories, there is a meta-awareness that the author isn't about to kill every main character in a gun blaze, so the stakes feel low. What is more interesting to me is the moral grey area surrounding the creation of the SPARTAN soldiers, the simultaneous intellectual genius/infant of Master Chief as a mission-driven killing machine, and what will eventually become an extremely interesting Oedipal relationship between Master Chief and Cortana. <br /><br />Unfortunately, the story of Reach is my favorite so far in the Halo canon, and I preferred the Reach video game's approach to the story to this one. For me, that means that the novels can't get much better plotwise unless they deviate from canon or head into some more ancillary events. We'll see how that goes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2385460939128667534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_191276658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191276658" />
    <a title="Mike Smith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5905953-mike-smith"><img alt="Mike Smith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422633883p2/5905953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/191276658?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike Smith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike Smith" href="/user/show/5905953-mike-smith">Mike Smith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5905953-mike-smith?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer191276658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6447861398148189883">This was a bit better than I expected for a book based on a video game. This is the prequel to the game Halo, which involves a cybernetically enhanced super-soldier battling aliens over possession of a massive ring in space built by a long-dead species. The plot is pretty thin and goes through some major contortions to get all the major characters where they need to be to begin the game. The characters themselves are fairly one-dimensional, with most of the soldiers being either cowards or noble</span>
  <span id="freeText6447861398148189883" style="display:none">This was a bit better than I expected for a book based on a video game. This is the prequel to the game Halo, which involves a cybernetically enhanced super-soldier battling aliens over possession of a massive ring in space built by a long-dead species. The plot is pretty thin and goes through some major contortions to get all the major characters where they need to be to begin the game. The characters themselves are fairly one-dimensional, with most of the soldiers being either cowards or noble, quick-thinking warriors. The book explains how the main character, Master Chief, came to be selected for the super-soldier project (at age six), his early training, and a few major missions. The action scenes were competently written and used enough visual cues from the game that you can imagine what the scenes looked like without having to go into excessive detail. The book nicely fills in some plot points and background for the game. Bottom line: if you played and liked the game, you'll probably enjoy the book. If you haven't played the game, you could give it a pass.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6447861398148189883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3489735465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3489735465" />
    <a title="Eric Allen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6229358-eric-allen"><img alt="Eric Allen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560117879p2/6229358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer7937191955110606139">I've been on a Halo kick lately, going through the story campaigns on all the older games. The original release versions. You know, the ones before 343 got their grubby fingers all over them, reconned the hell out of them, removed 2 player coop from the campaigns, (I mean, WTactualF, that was the funnest part, playing through the campaign, split screen, with a friend) and then turned Halo into a gigantic joke. 1-3, Reach, and ODST.   <span id="freeText7937191955110606139" style="display:none">I've been on a Halo kick lately, going through the story campaigns on all the older games. The original release versions. You know, the ones before 343 got their grubby fingers all over them, reconned the hell out of them, removed 2 player coop from the campaigns, (I mean, WTactualF, that was the funnest part, playing through the campaign, split screen, with a friend) and then turned Halo into a gigantic joke. 1-3, Reach, and ODST. All great games, and I don't even like shooters. I figured I'd read a couple of the books, especially the ones that deal with things outside of the games, but give important perspective on them, like this one.<br /><br /><br /><br />Aaaaaaaanyway. The book was okay. Like, the story and lore fills in a big chunk of the Halo universe, and it was good for that. But it's really boringly written in this flat, lifeless way, and pretty much every military cliche that exists makes at least one appearance in the book. It's really blandly and kind of badly written. The story could have probably been told better by a more talented author.</span>

<div id="review_2501773388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2501773388" />
    <a title="C.T. Phipps" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5873287-c-t-phipps"><img alt="C.T. Phipps" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401836765p2/5873287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2501773388?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.T. Phipps" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.T. Phipps" href="/user/show/5873287-c-t-phipps">C.T. Phipps</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5873287-c-t-phipps?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5873287-c-t-phipps?shelf=halo">halo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2501773388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10196511537370136638">I am a huge fan of the Halo universe and doubly-so it's Expanded Universe. Long before I got my copy of the Master Chief collection, I was enjoying the books by Eric Nylund and William Dietz that set up a surprisingly awesome science fiction universe. They were written in conunction with the original game and I suspect provided much of the backstory which would eventually be incorporated into the game's lore.<br/><br/>The premise is surprisingly dark. John-117 is a six-year-old boy kidnapped from his fami</span>
  <span id="freeText10196511537370136638" style="display:none">I am a huge fan of the Halo universe and doubly-so it's Expanded Universe. Long before I got my copy of the Master Chief collection, I was enjoying the books by Eric Nylund and William Dietz that set up a surprisingly awesome science fiction universe. They were written in conunction with the original game and I suspect provided much of the backstory which would eventually be incorporated into the game's lore.<br /><br />The premise is surprisingly dark. John-117 is a six-year-old boy kidnapped from his family by the Office of Naval Intelligence. Doctor Catherine Halsey proceeds to teach John and seventy-four other candidates bruttal combat techniques as well as strategy for the next decade. He is part of the SPARTAN-II program that is designed to produce super-soldiers. <br /><br />Rather than vilify her for, the books show the children thriving under their training until they are surgically enhanced to become cyborgs capable of wearing Mjolnir armor. It's just in time, too, because the human race is being invaded by the Covenant and they want to exterminate us. Determined to defend their home, the Spartans fight a desperate holding action against a foe with far more advanced technology.<br /><br />Despite the dark backstory, which helps it stand out from the rest, Halo: The Fall of Reach is a really entertaining action novel as well as uplifting. We see John and his Fireteam bond with one another as well as learn the lessons which will allow them to delay the Covenant even if they can't stop it. The action in the book is tremendous and the characters stand out. I liked Doctor Halsey a lot despite the fact she's a kidnapper, a mad scientist, and quite possibly crazy.<br /><br />The events of the books were so entertaining they've been adapted twice with Halo: The Fall of Reach as a CGI movie I first saw on netflix as well as a somewhat looser adaptation of the novel's second half in the Halo: Reach video game. I shouldn't give this book such a high score as I'm going to but I've read the books like three times now and will probably read them again, I haven't done that with any other book.<br /><br />10/10</span>
  <a data-text-id="10196511537370136638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1880312609876268595">Halo, The Fall of the Reach by Eric Nylund <br/>Summary, The Fall of Reach is a prequel telling the story of humanity's war against a technologically superior race called the Covenant, a mysterious race on a religious crusade to destroy all of humanity. The story focuses on the hero John and his fellow Spartans Sam, and Kelly enhanced human beings bred as soldiers for humanity's military and the best chance the humans have for victory in the losing war against the covenant. John, Sam and Kelly were k</span>
  <span id="freeText1880312609876268595" style="display:none">Halo, The Fall of the Reach by Eric Nylund <br />Summary, The Fall of Reach is a prequel telling the story of humanity's war against a technologically superior race called the Covenant, a mysterious race on a religious crusade to destroy all of humanity. The story focuses on the hero John and his fellow Spartans Sam, and Kelly enhanced human beings bred as soldiers for humanity's military and the best chance the humans have for victory in the losing war against the covenant. John, Sam and Kelly were kidnapped by Office of Navy Intelligent ONI for short, when they were kids and trained to be warriors. The story is told by the main person John, and has flash backs to and from the past. John is a strong man, who’s luck never runs out. He has seen a lot of combat, but still hold on to his human side. He cares for all of the members of the team, and will never leave his team in a bad situation. <br /><br />I enjoyed the book, this was the third Halo book, and they have also had a lot of video games and one cartoon movie. I would recommend this book to all who enjoy a good sci-fi novel. <br /><br />Eric Nylund is the author of Halo: The Fall of Reach, a novel that acts as a prequel to Halo: Combat Evolved, Halo: First Strike, a sequel to Halo: The Flood and prequel to Halo 2, and a sequel to Halo 2, Halo: Ghosts of Onyx. Eric Nylund actual job is as a writer for Microsoft Game Studios. His job is to develop character and story bibles, he write backstory, write game manuals, write game scripts.<br /></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1088075622?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/36225070-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36225070-nathan?shelf=want-to-reread">want-to-reread</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1088075622" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8824948983927560592"> Originally I thought the book was going to be some kind of, mash up of random killing and plain old combat like the games can be. Boy was I wrong. It is amazing how much actual story line and background they add to the rest of the books/games with just the one book!<br/><br/> I am aware that the author had to go into the game and possibly even look up different halo history to keep the book as accurate as possible, which can be a tough job. Even so the book was still written and done very well. Every tim</span>
  <span id="freeText8824948983927560592" style="display:none"> Originally I thought the book was going to be some kind of, mash up of random killing and plain old combat like the games can be. Boy was I wrong. It is amazing how much actual story line and background they add to the rest of the books/games with just the one book!<br /><br /> I am aware that the author had to go into the game and possibly even look up different halo history to keep the book as accurate as possible, which can be a tough job. Even so the book was still written and done very well. Every time there was a part that referenced to the game itself I would always try to predict what would happen next.<br /><br /> Something I think would have made it even better is if he took the book to the next level by adding in a few little sections here and there about the Spartans personal lives and relationships with each other and the people around them. They may be scientific engineered military weapons, but they are still people after all.<br /><br /> All in all the story was a lot better than I thought, and it got better as I continued, it wasn't rushed, it wasn't jumpy, and that is what makes it one of the best books I've ever read.<br /><br /> If you like your Science Fiction books, and especially war books and aliens, THIS is the book for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8824948983927560592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jesse Booth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jesse Booth" href="/user/show/1054882-jesse-booth">Jesse Booth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39681188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6430422769621983413">The Halo story is phenomenal. For people who just play the video games, you are missing out on the best part. Gameplay may be fun, but reading about the actual story completes the game.<br/><br/>Fall of Reach is a prequel to the original Halo: Combat Evolved story and gives amazing insight on how John 117 came to be. He definitely has more of a personality in the book, so it was good to actually see that.<br/><br/>As the title of the book indicates, this story goes into detail about the events leading up to when Th</span>
  <span id="freeText6430422769621983413" style="display:none">The Halo story is phenomenal. For people who just play the video games, you are missing out on the best part. Gameplay may be fun, but reading about the actual story completes the game.<br /><br />Fall of Reach is a prequel to the original Halo: Combat Evolved story and gives amazing insight on how John 117 came to be. He definitely has more of a personality in the book, so it was good to actually see that.<br /><br />As the title of the book indicates, this story goes into detail about the events leading up to when The Pillar of Autumn jumped into slipspace and escaped literal destruction from the devastation of Reach. Reach is the biggest military base humanity owns, and they fight valiantly, but the Covenant is just too powerful. They come full force at the planet and The Pillar of Autumn narrowly escapes. The book ends with the discovery of the first Halo ring, built by the forerunners.<br /><br />Eric Nylund is actually a decent writer. He keeps things interesting and consistent. I read this book about 6 years ago, but with the recent announcement of Halo: Reach, I wanted to go through the story again. I am glad I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6430422769621983413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13105095856700801914">I was reading the gaming blog Kotaku as my daily routine when I saw a live action trailer for the latest Halo game, Halo: Reach. I was taken away immediate and noticed one of the commentors said that if you like this trailer, you definitely have to read the book The Fall of Reach by Eric Nylund.<br/><br/>The only experience I've had with Halo so far was a few minutes watching my friend play Halo 2 at his place, and so had doubts of whether I will understand or enjoy the story.   <span id="freeText13105095856700801914" style="display:none">I was reading the gaming blog Kotaku as my daily routine when I saw a live action trailer for the latest Halo game, Halo: Reach. I was taken away immediate and noticed one of the commentors said that if you like this trailer, you definitely have to read the book The Fall of Reach by Eric Nylund.<br /><br />The only experience I've had with Halo so far was a few minutes watching my friend play Halo 2 at his place, and so had doubts of whether I will understand or enjoy the story. In the end I decided to give it a try due to strong user feedbacks and I am glad to say that it was a worthwhile decision.<br /><br />Nylund paints a thorough and vivid background of the Halo universe; from the beginnings of Master Chief as a child to his training and his battles with the Covenant. This is a good story for people who are interested in Science Fiction in general and not necessarily for fans of the games.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2805811544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer150095614215252044">I wasn't sure what I was heading into when I picked up this book.<br/><br/>I was expecting a lot of action. I wasn't sure how good the writing was going to be. I thought it would be fun, but not great. I thought it might feel too "gamey".<br/><br/>But it was actually a lot of fun, written well, and a really enjoyable read! Also emotional at times! It was action packed as hell, but in a great way. <br/><br/>I was pleasantly shocked, and will be keeping my eye out for the next two in the trilogy on my next bookstore trip.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3314813953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3314813953" />
    <a title="Stefan Gugler" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21258671-stefan-gugler"><img alt="Stefan Gugler" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577458544p2/21258671.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3314813953?book_show_action=true">May 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Gugler" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Gugler" href="/user/show/21258671-stefan-gugler">Stefan Gugler</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stefan by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/105052019-kayla-comalli">Kayla Comalli</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3314813953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8414240170459836574">It was much better than expected. Usually, video game books don't have such a great reputation, so I went in with a pretty low expectation. Yet I must admit that the pacing was quite agreeable and the level of detail didn't feel overwhelming, even though I'm new to the Halo universe. From time to time the whole militarism gets a bit trite and I can't read more about how proud and obedient Master Chief wants to be but generally, that was ok. Especially the first half felt a bit like Ender's Game,</span>
  <span id="freeText8414240170459836574" style="display:none">It was much better than expected. Usually, video game books don't have such a great reputation, so I went in with a pretty low expectation. Yet I must admit that the pacing was quite agreeable and the level of detail didn't feel overwhelming, even though I'm new to the Halo universe. From time to time the whole militarism gets a bit trite and I can't read more about how proud and obedient Master Chief wants to be but generally, that was ok. Especially the first half felt a bit like Ender's Game, the second half a bit like Star Wars. If you are interested in the Halo universe, I can definitely recommend.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3151106746" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3151106746" />
    <a title="Jared Bird" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13476472-jared-bird"><img alt="Jared Bird" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349703435p2/13476472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3151106746?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jared Bird" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jared Bird" href="/user/show/13476472-jared-bird">Jared Bird</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3151106746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1435035365739313093">The book begins expertly enough, with a number of memorable scenes involving the Spartan's formation and training. The characters are well written and consistent with their video game counterparts, in the situations where that's appropriate. John, Spartan 117, is especially faithful. He's a soldier, through and through, with enough character to make him likeable and understandable, but not so much that you forget that he's the main protagonist of the video game. The details of the book are great</span>
  <span id="freeText1435035365739313093" style="display:none">The book begins expertly enough, with a number of memorable scenes involving the Spartan's formation and training. The characters are well written and consistent with their video game counterparts, in the situations where that's appropriate. John, Spartan 117, is especially faithful. He's a soldier, through and through, with enough character to make him likeable and understandable, but not so much that you forget that he's the main protagonist of the video game. The details of the book are great, especially considering the author had to flesh out a lot of details of the universe that aren't readily available in the game.<br /><br />This book suffers from a few set backs though - one of the most notable for me was in terms of believability. I know there's the suspension of disbelief that exists for almost all forms of media, but in this case, we were taken to believe that a child has the reflexes to pull a coin out of midair and tell you which side is facing up. This child is then trained in the military to increase upon his natural talents. As a youth, he's given serums, surgeries, and treatments to augment those abilities even further. Then, he's given a suit of armor that makes him even stronger and faster. They then upgrade this same suit of armor [i]again[/i], which felt incredibly redundant. Lastly, they add in an artificial intelligence to increase his reflexes. By this point, he must be able to see into the future. It feels so hokey and redundant that I didn't bother trying to understand it. I played the game - Master Chief is good, but he's not a deity.<br /><br />Secondly, pacing. The book spends a long time meandering about, and not really getting to the point. The book is called "The Fall of Reach". We know how it ends. How it gets there is very consuming and not altogether rewarding. The best aspect of the book though is [spoiler] how the Master Chief was actually intended to be going on a mission to destroy the covenant at the very moment that Reach was invaded, showing that humanity was ready to take some initiative in this fight just before being dealt a crippling blow, and giving good reason for why the Master Chief was in the situation he's in at the beginning of Halo: Combat Evolved [/spoiler].<br /><br />Admittedly, I forgot when this book was written and wanted to read this book because I wanted some insight into Reach after having played Halo: Reach on PC. There was certainly none of that here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1435035365739313093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7UAI6s6663wCbfZ2vdM4GLaqJxFyrrOkCIfqJuzSfxYxagJrHMSCf8bfS4WgmBFMHwZ4RVJxchCKxrqVBzzRGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XH9nA03/LKsdqiN339ECv33KsyQHVspe7y+aIpjpU4aAVW2Cn4FFqNkYnoTCmivr1GbscCeJC+ptbsqRcwf9iQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
